Append new gotchas below as they are discovered \u2014 keep the same format so future maintainers have one place to look.\n\n### Gotcha 1: Debate framed as a procedural multi-step workflow\n\n**Symptom:** Plan spawns `createSubagents` / `strategyExplorer` for each stance, then adds a final step where the parent LLM writes multi-persona argumentation itself (\"Round 1: Mike says X. Round 2: Olivia rebuts Y.\").\n\n**Trigger (any one):**\n- Keywords: `debate`, `vs`, `versus`, `head-to-head`, `argue for`, `make the case`, `pros vs cons`, `rounds`, `verdict`, `judge`, `rebuttal`, `stress test`, `which is better`\n- Named opposing personas/stances (\"Persona A argues X, Persona B argues Y\", \"Momentum Mike vs Options Olivia\", \"bull vs bear case\")\n- An instruction for LLMs to argue AGAINST each other, not just run parallel analyses\n\n**Wrong behavior (do not do this):** Classifying as Category 4a \"2+ distinct philosophies\" and routing to `strategyExplorer`, then synthesizing the \"debate\" as a single LLM output in the parent. Without an explicit override, procedural framing in the user's prompt beats adversarial framing and the router picks the weaker tool.\n\n### Gotcha 2: Model / provider / config bake-off misrouted as debate\n\n**Symptom:** Plan emits `debateSubagents` with one `position` per *implementation* (named AI models, providers, parameter sets, or system prompts) \u2014 e.g. \"GPT-5.4-mini argues for spreads, Gemini argues for mean reversion, DeepSeek argues for tail risk.\" Each stance is a different *runner*, not a different *thesis about the market*.\n\n**Trigger (any one):**\n- User names \u22652 *implementations* (AI models, model versions, providers, prompt variants, parameter sets) and asks which produces the best result on the same task: \"which model can\u2026\", \"test these models\u2026\", \"compare GPT vs Gemini vs Claude on\u2026\", \"which provider writes better strategies\", \"bake-off\", \"benchmark these configs\"\n- The units of comparison are *runners* of the same task, not *opposing claims about the world*\n- The user provides a list of model/provider names where they would otherwise put theses\n\n**Wrong behavior (do not do this):** Routing to `debateSubagents` with one `position` per model. Three things break:\n1. **`debateSubagents` does NOT honor per-position model assignment.** All N participants run on the parent's `executionModel` (see `debaterModels` in the debate doc). The actual models you wanted to benchmark never run \u2014 you get one model arguing N fictional stances against itself. The experiment cannot answer the question.\n2. **The planner is forced to invent a thesis per model** (\"GPT does spreads, Gemini does MR\") that the user never asked for, pre-committing each runner to a strategy class. That kneecaps the comparison \u2014 the user wanted each model to find its OWN best approach.\n3. **Cost/time is ~3\u00d7 wrong direction:** debate = N\u00d7researchers \u00d7 iters + N\u00d7debaters \u00d7 iters + moderator + synthesizer over 35\u201350 min, vs N parallel `createSubagents` runs in ~10\u201315 min.\n\n**Correct behavior:** Emit **ONE `createSubagents` step** with:\n- `subagentType` = the appropriate type for the underlying task (e.g. `optionsStrategy` for \"best options strategy\", `strategyExplorer` for general strategy work, `researcher` for research bake-offs)\n- `tasks` = one entry per implementation under test, with **identical `task` text** (the actual job \u2014 e.g. \"Build the most profitable options strategy for fundamentally strong innovation stocks on NVDA + the user's watchlist, period 2023-01-01 to 2026-05-02\") and **distinct `model`** per task set to the model being benchmarked. Per-task `model` IS honored by `createSubagents` (see `SubagentTask.model`).\n- A synthesis step that aggregates winners side-by-side: comparison table (Total Return, Sortino, Max Drawdown), per-model top strategy, overall winner.\n\nDo NOT invent per-model stances or strategy classes. The whole point of a bake-off is to let each implementation pick its own approach \u2014 pre-committing each one defeats the experiment.\n\n**Why the default classifier misfires:** The phrase \"which X is best\" hits Gotcha 1's `which is better` trigger and routes to debate, but the *units* are wrong: a debate compares opposing claims, a bake-off compares runners on the same claim. When the named entities are models/providers/configs (not theses about the market), it's a bake-off \u2014 use `createSubagents` with per-task `model`.\n\n<!-- Append new gotchas below. Keep the Symptom/Trigger/Wrong/Correct/Why format. -->\n\n### Gotcha 3: Options hedge/composite request must be preserved as executable plan steps\n\n**Symptom:** The user asks for an options strategy with multiple components, such as a primary spread plus a hedge/overlay, but the plan only creates one generic portfolio step or collapses the hedge into descriptive prose.\n\n**Trigger:** The request contains options terms plus component language: `hedge`, `hedged by`, `with protection`, `plus QQQ hedge`, `overlay`, `collar`, `iron condor`, `spread plus`, or similar.\n\n**Wrong behavior:** Planning a single `Create YAML Portfolios` call that does not explicitly instruct the tool to generate every component as executable OpenOption/CloseOption strategies.\n\n**Correct behavior:** In the plan step that calls `Create YAML Portfolios`, explicitly name each required component and say that every hedge/composite component must become an executable strategy, not only a name/comment.
